# Current Sprint

## Sprint Goal

Make the Obsidian vault the source of truth for design and tracking, then continue implementation from a clear HLD/LLD and retrieval-intelligence plan.

## Done

- Corrected the frontend live-smoke proof formatter for the accepted OpenRouter path. A failing frontend regression first showed the current `openrouter-livekit` smoke ledger, which carries `reasoning_model_id=deepseek/deepseek-v4-flash` and `reasoning_ttft_ms`, would still render as `Gemma/Kokoro transport` and omit the OpenRouter TTFT/model evidence. The formatter now labels current proof evidence as `OpenRouter/Kokoro transport`, renders `OpenRouter TTFT`, and shows `Reasoning: deepseek/deepseek-v4-flash` while preserving legacy Gemma labels for explicit legacy smoke steps. Frontend verification passed `npm run test:race`, `npm run typecheck`, `npm run lint`, and `npm run build`.
- Hardened PR hygiene for local scratch checkouts and lockfile handling. A failing-first repo workflow guard showed the root `repo_check_temp/` scratch checkout was not explicitly ignored even though it contains course checkout files, PDFs, snapshots, and a nested `.git`; `.gitignore` now excludes only `/repo_check_temp/` under scratch research/course work. `tests/test_repo_workflow_ci.py` verifies the anchored ignore rule, CI `uv sync --locked` usage, and that `uv.lock` remains tracked/not ignored, so bulky artifacts stay local while the intended Python lockfile remains in the PR surface.
- Removed another live-voice reopening trap from the proof handoff. A red regression showed current vault knowledge graph surfaces could still say the OpenRouter LiveKit path needed an accepted proof record, and the UUID operator input template labeled live-voice defaults as proof blockers. The system-design knowledge graph, architecture map, objective audit, and operator-input template now state that provider-backed live voice is accepted and reserve blocker language for the remaining external publication inputs. Focused regressions passed with `2 passed`.
- Fixed the accepted proof audit-note path portability leak from the latest Leibniz review. A failing regression first showed `_provider_proof_record_audit_note` could emit the local checkout root in `workspace_validation_report_artifact_id` and `preflight_validation_report_artifact_id`; audit value serialization now normalizes project-root paths to `<workspace-root>/...`, and the tracked accepted live-voice audit notes in the project/system-design vault handoffs were corrected. Focused proof regressions passed with `3 passed`; ruff passed for the touched proof/CI files.

Accepted live-voice commands stay excluded. Refreshed the ignored UUID proof packets and static proof surfaces locally.

The latest Cursor notes report that live dialogue no longer depends on local MLX servers on `:8080`/`:8090` or `GEMMA4_MULTIMODAL_ENDPOINT_URL`; reasoning is now OpenRouter text chat (`deepseek/deepseek-v4-flash`) with LiveKit transport and Kokoro spoken output, using the Live Voice panel text-turn composer. - Added project-memory and publish-readiness durable event redaction. Failing-first API regressions showed `project_memory_recorded`, publish-readiness `feedback_recorded`, and `publish_readiness_checked` events could persist raw project memory content, sensitive metadata, and unsupported publish-channel strings containing Bearer/HF-shaped values. `ProjectMemoryWorkflow` and `PublishReadinessWorkflow` now apply `safe_realtime_metadata` at those durable event boundaries, and Bearer redaction is case-insensitive so normalized publish-channel names cannot preserve lower-case bearer tokens. Private memory storage, private feedback storage, and publish-readiness API responses remain unchanged. Focused coverage passed with `2 passed`. This hardens trace/privacy boundaries only; live voice is now accepted and external publication proof remains blocked.
- Added feedback and memory durable event redaction. The failing-first regression showed `feedback_recorded`, `feedback_routed`, and `memory_recorded` events could persist raw human feedback text, author strings, target artifact titles, memory content, and sensitive metadata containing Bearer/HF/Tavily-shaped values. `FeedbackRoutingWorkflow`, `RevisionWorkflow`, and the direct `/api/memories` record path now apply `safe_realtime_metadata` at those event boundaries, preserving private stored feedback, routed A2A messages, and agent memories while redacting durable event payload strings and dropping sensitive metadata keys. Focused feedback/memory redaction coverage passed with `3 passed`, and the broader feedback/routing/A2A subset passed with `43 passed`. The workspace path now also fails closed for non-directory and broken-symlink ancestors instead of raising. `product_run_bootstrap` and the blocked concrete README now point to this command. This still does not create live provider proof or external publication proof.
- Closed the Leibniz UUID-gate follow-up for provider proof. Review confirmed no Critical or Important findings after non-UUID run ids were blocked across proof template generation, record validation, preflight validation, workspace init/validation, completion status, and the checked-in `RUN-2026-05-20-NEXT` workspace. Final local verification: provider proof tests `178 passed`, foundation `21 passed`, browser/static proof surfaces `14 passed` outside the sandbox after the expected Chromium Mach-port sandbox failure, `compileall` passed, and focused stale-command plus whitespace/control-character scans passed.
- Hardened accepted provider-backed live voice proof records against preflight runtime-check drift. Red regressions first proved a hand-edited accepted live-voice audit note could claim valid preflight while listing only four of the five required runtime checks, and then that extra non-generated runtime-check names could still be accepted. Preflight validation reports now carry canonical `validated_runtime_checks`, record validation requires the exact generated required-check sequence, compact proof audit notes preserve `preflight_validation_report_validated_runtime_checks`, and proof-plan/static voice surfaces now require that linkage. This still does not configure providers, run LiveKit/Gemma/Kokoro, create accepted proof, or complete the objective.
- Hardened accepted external publication proof records against preflight/destination channel drift. A red regression first proved an accepted `external-publication-proof` record could point `destination_channel` at `x_thread` while the accepted preflight validation report only validated `linkedin`; record validation now carries `validated_publish_channels` from `publish-readiness.preflight.json`, requires the accepted record destination channel to appear there, emits `destination_channel_missing_from_preflight`, records the validated channel list into compact audit notes, and keeps the concrete `RUN-2026-05-20-NEXT` proof workspace/regression snapshots current. This still does not perform live publication or create accepted proof.
- Hardened external publication preflight validation against duplicate, alias-duplicate, blank, or unsupported channel checks. Red regressions first proved a ready `publish-readiness.preflight.json` with two `linkedin` channel checks, alias-equivalent `x` and `twitter` checks, or an unsupported `mastodon` channel could still emit preflight artifact IDs; validation now normalizes publish-channel aliases, emits `publish_channel_duplicate_platform` or `publish_channel_platform_unsupported`, withholds artifact IDs, and proof-plan surfaces require one normalized, non-empty supported `publish_channel_checks` entry per channel. After `Leibniz` review, blank or whitespace-only channel platforms now emit `publish_channel_platform_missing` and also withhold artifact IDs.
- Hardened live voice preflight validation against duplicate required runtime check IDs. Red regression first proved a duplicated ready `livekit-transport` check could mask an earlier blocked check with the same ID; `validate-provider-proof-preflight-artifacts` now emits `voice_runtime_duplicate_check_id`, withholds preflight artifact IDs, and the proof-plan requirement text says required runtime checks must be present once and ready. After `Leibniz` review, duplicate-check issue paths no longer interpolate captured `check_id` values, so token-shaped duplicate IDs cannot leak through validation JSON.
- Hardened external publication preflight policy semantics. Red regressions first proved `validate-provider-proof-preflight-artifacts` could accept contradictory publication preflight payloads that reported `ready` while a channel policy check still had `policy_status=needs_review`, reported `ready` while a channel still carried blocking issues, reported policy-review-only `needs_review` while every channel policy was already acknowledged, duplicated the policy-review blocker while still passing the set-based check, hid a non-policy channel blocker inside the policy-review handoff, or kept a policy-review blocker on an already acknowledged channel. Publication preflight validation now requires `policy_status=acknowledged` plus no top-level or channel blocking issues when the overall publish readiness status is `ready`; the `needs_review` handoff requires the exact single top-level policy-review blocker, only empty or policy-review channel blockers, at least one pending channel policy, and no policy-review blocker on acknowledged channels.
- Fixed stale source-research status in the creator-facing Source panel. Red regressions first showed a stale blocked web-research message could keep the rail in `Research blocked` after a newer `web_research_completed` event recorded provider-backed sources, a malformed message timestamp could mask valid event evidence, and a higher-id malformed blocked event could mask a valid completed event. `sourceResearchStatus` now parses timestamps for message/event ordering, orders events by valid `created_at` before `event_id`, falls back conservatively when needed, still lets newer active messages keep the rail in `Research queued`, and disables `Run web research` while provider-backed research is already running.

- Added no-secret closure-review audit recording. `tests/test_provider_proof_plan_cli.py` first failed because validated closure-review records had no vault audit bridge; `record-provider-proof-closure-review` now validates filled review records, appends compact redacted audit notes, refuses invalid reviews without writing, preserves separate proof-audit targets for completion-status rechecks, and keeps `state_change_allowed=false`.
- Allowed meaningful rejected closure-review records. Leibniz found `valid_rejected_closure_review` was unreachable when a reviewer rejected closure because one requirement failed; rejected closure-review records now allow confirmed/rejected requirement values, require at least one rejected requirement, and keep blocker-state updates disallowed.
- Added no-secret closure-review validator for accepted provider proof. `tests/test_provider_proof_plan_cli.py` first failed because filled closure-review records had no validator; `validate-provider-proof-closure-review` now rechecks completion status, validates reviewer decision, timestamp, accepted proof/source linkage, review requirements, redaction proof, and token-shaped values without changing blocker state. The closure-review template now includes the validation command with active audit-target overrides.
- Preserved audit-target overrides in provider proof closure-review commands. Leibniz found accepted completion status could be produced from `--audit-target` overrides but then emit a closure-review template command that rechecked default vault targets; the emitted `provider-proof-closure-review-template` command now appends every active audit-target override with shell-safe quoting, and regression coverage proves paths containing spaces remain reproducible.
- Added no-secret closure-review template command for accepted provider proof. `tests/test_provider_proof_plan_cli.py` first failed because accepted `provider-proof-completion-status` did not point to a durable reviewer-fillable record; `provider-proof-closure-review-template` now emits a template only after completion status is `required_proofs_accepted`, blocks when accepted proof is missing, and keeps `state_change_allowed=false`. Accepted completion status now surfaces the template command while keeping blocker mutation outside the status/template commands.
- Added closure-review handoff to provider proof completion status. `tests/test_provider_proof_plan_cli.py` first failed because `required_proofs_accepted` did not expose the next reviewed blocker-closure step; `provider-proof-completion-status` now returns top-level `next_action=prepare_blocker_closure_review`, no state-changing commands, and a no-secret `closure_review_packet` with accepted proof sources, required review checks, and candidate blocker states after reviewer approval while keeping `blocker_state_change_allowed_by_this_command=false`.
- Added next-action proof commands to provider proof completion status. `tests/test_provider_proof_plan_cli.py` first failed because `provider-proof-completion-status` reported missing proof records without carrying the exact next operator commands; each proof status now includes `next_action`, `next_action_commands`, and `record_proof_in`, so blocked operators can generate the proof template, validate captured JSON, record the audit note, and rerun completion status from the same no-secret status packet. Leibniz found the `blocked_by_run_id` early return still omitted the new fields; placeholder and unsafe run ids now expose the same shape with `<run-id>` substituted in commands and `replace_run_id_and_recheck` as the next action.
- Blocked secret-shaped provider proof run ids before command generation. Leibniz found token-shaped strings that matched the run-id character whitelist could still be treated as concrete and echoed into proof-plan/completion-status commands; run-id classification now treats `PROVIDER_PROOF_SECRET_VALUE_PATTERN` matches as `unsafe_run_id`, run-id status takes precedence before credential blockers, and completion status sanitizes unsafe `run_id` output to `<run-id>`.
- Sanitized secret-shaped run ids in provider proof workspace initialization. Leibniz found `init-provider-proof-workspace` still echoed raw token-shaped run ids in its blocked payload; workspace payloads now use the proof plan's safe `command_run_id`, so token-shaped unsafe run ids are reported as `<run-id>` and no workspace files are written.
- Closed duplicate-field bypass in provider proof completion-status audit notes. Leibniz found `_provider_proof_audit_note_fields()` collapsed duplicate Markdown keys with `setdefault`, so later contradictory or secret-shaped duplicate fields were invisible. New regressions first reproduced both bypasses; audit-note parsing now preserves ordered field entries for secret scanning, treats duplicate accepted-note fields as invalid accepted evidence, and keeps the collapsed first-value map only for legacy field lookup.
- Required schema-backed accepted audit-note fields in provider proof completion status. Leibniz found accepted Markdown notes could omit required live voice session/config fields or publication policy/rollback fields while still reporting completion; accepted audit notes now compare their parsed fields against the proof schema's audit-emitted required fields and block as invalid accepted evidence when required values are missing, empty, or still template placeholders.
- Required accepted audit notes to preserve validation summary and redaction proof. Leibniz found hand-edited notes could claim `valid_accepted_record` while omitting the emitted `post_capture_validation_results` and `secret_redaction_check`; completion status now requires the validation summary to match the expected check count with zero failures and requires the redaction check to be passed/true.
- Required parseable provider-proof validation timestamps. Leibniz found accepted JSON proof records and accepted audit notes could use non-parseable `validation_timestamp` values while still counting as valid; validation now emits `invalid_validation_timestamp`, and completion status treats accepted audit notes with unparseable validation timestamps as invalid accepted evidence.
- Prevented malformed invalid/secret audit notes from being masked by older accepted notes. Leibniz found an older parseable accepted note could hide a later hand-edited accepted note with an unparseable timestamp plus invalid fields or secret-shaped values; completion status now treats unorderable invalid/secret accepted markers conservatively so they block instead of disappearing behind older accepted evidence.
- Blocked invalid accepted audit-note fields in provider proof completion status. `tests/test_provider_proof_plan_cli.py` first failed because a hand-edited accepted `external-publication-proof` audit note could set `destination_channel=linkedin` while pointing `durable_platform_id_or_url` to Instagram and still satisfy completion status; `provider-proof-completion-status` now returns `blocked_by_invalid_accepted_audit_note`, emits `accepted_audit_note_invalid_fields`, reports `invalid_accepted_audit_note_proofs`, marks the proof as `latest_record_has_invalid_fields`, and preserves `invalid_source_targets` without clearing blockers or echoing secrets.
- Rejected cross-channel accepted publication proof records. `tests/test_provider_proof_plan_cli.py` first failed because an accepted `external-publication-proof` record could set `destination_channel=linkedin` while pointing `durable_platform_id_or_url` to Instagram, X, or Substack; validation now emits `destination_channel_mismatch` when a known platform URL/URN contradicts the selected channel, while preserving matching platform URLs and opaque unknown external evidence. Leibniz review then found repo-canonical aliases were over-blocked; `instagram_post`, `instagram_reel`, and `x_thread` now normalize to their platform families before comparison.
- Blocked local or draft destinations from accepted publication proof records. `tests/test_provider_proof_plan_cli.py` first failed because an accepted `external-publication-proof` record could use `file://`, localhost, or local draft-preview evidence as `durable_platform_id_or_url`; validation now rejects those local/internal substitutes with `durable_destination_not_external` while still allowing failed records to be recorded as failure evidence. Leibniz review then found private/link-local/unspecified IPs plus home, relative, Windows, dotless, reserved/internal DNS, non-proof URL schemes, and short draft/preview/internal markers still passed; the classifier now accepts only external `http(s)` URLs or explicit opaque platform IDs such as `urn:li:share:123`. A follow-up review found valid external slugs containing `local` or `internal` were over-blocked; marker rejection is now limited to opaque evidence and explicit `/draft` or `/preview` URL paths.
- Required runtime-health voice-edge benchmark evidence in live voice proof plans. `tests/test_provider_proof_plan_cli.py` first failed because live voice proof commands skipped `build-runtime-health-ledger`; `provider-proof-plan`, proof readiness, and the OpenRouter LiveKit voice boundary map now require a same-run `runtime_health_ledger` with `voice-edge-local-benchmark` ready status, add `runtime_health_ledger_artifact_id` and `voice_edge_benchmark_status` to the live voice proof record schema, and keep provider-backed voice blocked until that local edge proof is recorded before live smoke/timing evidence. Leibniz review then found accepted records could contradict the checklist with `voice_edge_benchmark_status=failed`; validation now rejects accepted live-voice records unless the benchmark status is `ready`, `execute_live_calls` is true, and `realtime_provider` is `gemma4_realtime`.
- Blocked secret-shaped audit notes in provider proof completion status. `tests/test_provider_proof_plan_cli.py` first failed because a manually edited accepted audit note containing token-shaped text could still satisfy completion; `provider-proof-completion-status` now returns `blocked_by_secret_shaped_audit_note`, emits `audit_note_secret_shape_detected`, reports only proof IDs and target paths, and does not echo the matched value. Leibniz review then found failed/missing proof states could mask the secret-shaped status; regressions now verify secret-shaped notes keep top-level precedence while preserving the other issue codes.
- Required matching proof artifact types in provider proof completion status. `tests/test_provider_proof_plan_cli.py` first failed because accepted-looking audit notes with swapped `proof_artifact_type` values could satisfy completion; `provider-proof-completion-status` now ignores accepted/failed audit notes unless `proof_artifact_type` matches the selected proof schema.
- Added self-audit fields to provider proof completion status. `tests/test_provider_proof_plan_cli.py` first failed because completion-status payloads did not expose the required proof IDs or state-change boundary; `provider-proof-completion-status` now includes `required_proofs`, `completion_requirements`, `state_change_boundary`, and `blocker_state_change_allowed_by_this_command=false` so even a green status remains explicitly status-only until a separate reviewed state update.
- Anchored provider proof completion-status latest-record selection to validation timestamps. `tests/test_provider_proof_plan_cli.py` first failed because manual audit-note reordering could let an older accepted record appear later in the file and override a newer failed record; `provider-proof-completion-status` now prefers parseable `validation_timestamp` values for latest accepted/failed record selection, with file order only as a tie/fallback.
- Tightened provider proof completion-status latest-record semantics. `tests/test_provider_proof_plan_cli.py` first failed because an older accepted audit note could still report completion after a later failed proof record for the same proof/run; `provider-proof-completion-status` now classifies the latest valid accepted/failed audit note per proof and readable target, returns `blocked_by_latest_failed_proof_record` with `latest_proof_record_failed`, and reports per-proof `failed_source_targets` until a later accepted record supersedes the failure.
- Tightened provider proof completion-status target coverage. `tests/test_provider_proof_plan_cli.py` first failed because an accepted proof note in one configured audit target could report completion even when another readable audit target lacked the note; `provider-proof-completion-status` now reports `blocked_by_incomplete_audit_target_coverage`, `audit_target_coverage_incomplete`, and per-proof `missing_source_targets` until accepted live voice and publication proof notes are present in every configured readable audit target.
- Propagated provider proof completion-status commands into proof-plan exports. `tests/test_provider_proof_plan_cli.py` and `tests/test_blocker_snapshot_consistency.py` first failed because proof plans did not expose `completion_status_commands`; `provider-proof-plan`, proof readiness, and the OpenRouter LiveKit voice/publication boundary maps now carry and render `provider-proof-completion-status --run-id <run-id>` alongside template and record commands so operators can check the final accepted-proof audit state from every proof surface.
- Added a no-secret provider proof completion-status checker. `tests/test_provider_proof_plan_cli.py` first failed because `_provider_proof_completion_status_payload` did not exist; the CLI now has `provider-proof-completion-status` to scan configured audit targets for valid accepted live voice and publication proof-record notes for a durable product UUID run id, report missing accepted proof records plus missing/invalid audit targets without changing blocker state, and the proof workspace README points operators to that check after recording both proofs. Leibniz review then found malformed accepted-like markers and directory targets could produce false status/crashes; the checker now parses exact audit fields and treats non-file targets as invalid.
- Added a no-secret provider proof workspace initializer. `tests/test_provider_proof_plan_cli.py` first failed because `_provider_proof_workspace_payload` did not exist; the CLI now has `init-provider-proof-workspace` to create a run-specific output directory with both proof-record template JSON files plus a short README containing validate/record commands, while refusing placeholder/unsafe run ids without writing. Leibniz review then found reruns could overwrite partially filled proof files; the initializer now fails closed as `workspace_exists` with zero writes when any target template or README already exists.
- Added no-secret provider proof-record templates. `tests/test_provider_proof_plan_cli.py` first failed because `_provider_proof_record_template_payload` did not exist; the CLI now has `provider-proof-record-template` to emit a product-UUID-only draft JSON record with required schema fields and post-capture validation keys, while keeping placeholder/unsafe/non-UUID run ids blocked and keeping generated drafts invalid until real validation evidence replaces template placeholders.
- Added a no-secret provider proof-record audit bridge. `tests/test_provider_proof_plan_cli.py` first failed because `_record_provider_proof_record_payload` and proof-plan `record_commands` did not exist; the CLI now has `record-provider-proof-record` to validate captured accepted/failed proof JSON, append compact redacted Markdown notes to the project audit, active context, and system-design audit mirror, refuse invalid records or placeholder/unsafe run ids without writing, and expose the recording command in CLI/proof-readiness/OpenRouter LiveKit voice/publication boundary proof-plan exports.
- Added a no-secret provider proof-record validator. `tests/test_provider_proof_plan_cli.py` first failed because `_provider_proof_record_validation_payload` did not exist; the CLI now has `validate-provider-proof-record` to check captured proof JSON against the selected proof schema, run id, outcome, required post-capture validation results, and token-shaped value scan without changing blocker state.
- Added proof-artifact schemas to provider proof plans. `tests/test_provider_proof_plan_cli.py` first failed because future accepted/failed proof records had no stable schema; the CLI, proof-readiness export, and OpenRouter LiveKit voice/publication boundary maps now carry `proof_artifact_schema` with artifact type, allowed outcomes, blocker state field, and required no-secret fields for live voice and publication proof records.
- Added success-recording requirements to provider proof plans. `tests/test_provider_proof_plan_cli.py` first failed because passing runtime/publication proof had no explicit state-transition record; the CLI, proof-readiness export, and OpenRouter LiveKit voice/publication boundary maps now carry `success_recording_requirements` for run/check/validation time, artifact ids, passed validation checks, blocker-state update timing, and follow-up closure/linkage.
- Added failure-recording requirements to provider proof plans. `tests/test_provider_proof_plan_cli.py` first failed because failed runtime/publication proof attempts had no explicit feedback path; the CLI, proof-readiness export, and OpenRouter LiveKit voice/publication boundary maps now carry `failure_recording_requirements` for run/check time, failed step, redacted provider or platform context, blocked-state preservation, and follow-up task creation.
- Added post-capture validation checks to provider proof plans. `tests/test_provider_proof_plan_cli.py` first failed because proof packets lacked validation checks for comparing captured artifacts; the CLI, proof-readiness export, and OpenRouter LiveKit voice/publication boundary maps now carry `post_capture_validation_checks` for live-call flags, provider/session/run linkage, required timing/evidence, destination ID/URL linkage, and no-secret captured artifacts.
- Added proof-linkage requirements to provider proof plans. `tests/test_provider_proof_plan_cli.py` first failed because the CLI proof packets lacked same-run/session/destination linkage requirements; the CLI, proof-readiness export, and OpenRouter LiveKit voice/publication boundary maps now carry `proof_linkage_requirements` so accepted proof must tie live voice ledgers to the same run/session and publication evidence to the same destination ID or URL.
- Added rejected-substitute guardrails to provider proof plans. `tests/test_provider_proof_plan_cli.py` first failed because the CLI proof packets named accepted captures without naming rejected substitutes; the CLI, proof-readiness export, and OpenRouter LiveKit voice/publication boundary maps now reject credential-only, rehearsal, HF text-route, non-live smoke, generic policy, and local-draft substitutes.
- Exposed the safe command run id in provider proof plans. `tests/test_provider_proof_plan_cli.py` first failed because the payload exposed only run-id state; the CLI, proof-readiness export, and OpenRouter LiveKit voice/publication boundary maps now carry `command_run_id`, which is either the accepted durable product run UUID or `<run-id>` after placeholder/unsafe/non-UUID substitution.
- Added unsafe-run-id guarding to provider proof plans. `tests/test_provider_proof_plan_cli.py` first failed because a run id containing shell-control syntax still produced `ready_for_runtime_attempt`; the CLI now reports `unsafe_run_id`, blocks runtime attempt, and substitutes `<run-id>` in generated command/preflight text.

- Tightened accepted-source independence host grouping. The normalization strips repeated `www.`, removes simple host ports, canonicalizes IP literals, and handles common country-code second-level public suffixes such as `co.uk`, `co.nz`, `com.au`, and `co.za` conservatively without adding a runtime dependency. `Leibniz` found two real first-pass issues: unlisted country suffixes could collapse unrelated domains such as `vendor-a.co.nz` and `vendor-b.co.nz`, and IPv4 literals could collapse to partial labels such as `113.10`; both are fixed with regressions, and `Leibniz` closure review found no actionable findings. Validation passed failing-first country-suffix and IP regressions (`6 passed` targeted source-independence cases), focused retrieval/claim/publish graph tests (`18 passed`), compileall, full default backend regression (`457 passed, 11 expected infra skips`), host-context live Postgres regression (`468 passed`), no-SQLite adapter scan, high-entropy token scan, screenshot-location scan, and whitespace scan.
- Added accepted-source independence as a retrieval-quality recall gate. The ledger now records a `source_independence:host` graph gap when enough accepted evidence exists but every accepted source resolves to the same normalized host, marks accepted candidates with `single_host_source_cluster`, recommends independent source corroboration, keeps the ledger in `needs_more_recall`, and withholds downstream accepted-retrieval evidence until an independently hosted source is added. Ready-path tests and source-refresh fixtures now use independently hosted accepted evidence. Validation passed the failing-first single-host regression, focused retrieval/claim/publish graph tests (`19 passed`), compileall, full default backend regression (`452 passed, 11 expected infra skips`), host-context live Postgres regression (`463 passed`), no-SQLite adapter scan, high-entropy token scan, screenshot-location scan, whitespace scan, and `Leibniz` whole-slice review with no actionable findings. Residual policy note: official/vendor-primary-source-only topics now need an explicit source-policy waiver if the product wants to bypass this independence gate later.
- Added stricter retrieval-quality recall, contradiction, and graph traversal gates. Accepted evidence can no longer make a run `ready` when all accepted sources came from one normalized query and one retriever signal, when accepted evidence is missing query/retriever metadata, or when supported claim/artifact graph paths point only to unaccepted source dependencies. Candidate metadata can now mark contradiction status, explicit truthy `contradicts` flags, valid claim-level contradiction ids, or pending contradiction review; string false values and malformed claim ids are ignored; real contradiction sources receive contradiction precision risks, are excluded from accepted context, and keep the ledger in `needs_rerank` when enough clean accepted evidence remains. The ledger records `retrieval_diversity` gaps, marks accepted candidates with diversity recall risks, verifies claim/artifact overlap against accepted retrieval source ids, accepts `claim_dependency_ids`, `content.claim_ids`, and `provenance.claim_ids` as artifact claim contracts while ignoring malformed historical values, increments recall gaps, and recommends independent corroborating / alternate primary-evidence / claim-verification / contradictory-evidence-review queries. Downstream accepted-retrieval evidence is withheld unless source evidence is ready, but clean accepted sources still support claim verification when only rejected candidates need rerank review or when claim/artifact graph nodes are waiting for rewrite/verification. Publish readiness records `retrieval_quality_not_ready`, Autopilot blocks on every non-ready retrieval-quality status, source-ledger snapshots report non-ready retrieval status instead of `accepted_evidence_available`, and both initial provider-backed sources plus worker web-search sources persist `retriever=web_search`. The provider-free demo seed uses distinct seeded queries/retrievers so complete demo review state still proves the stricter contract. Validation passed failing-first diversity and metadata regressions, downstream claim/publish gate regression, clean-accepted `needs_rerank` regression, accepted-evidence graph traversal regression, contract-variant artifact claim-id regression from `Leibniz`, contradiction regression, false/malformed contradiction metadata regression, focused retrieval/claim/publish graph tests (`18 passed`), broader source-refresh/retrieval/project-memory/autonomous-pass/publish tests from the prior retrieval slice (`20 passed`), frontend source race suite from the UI-unchanged slice (`188 passed`), compileall, default backend regression (`451 passed, 11 expected infra skips`), host-context live Postgres full regression (`462 passed`), no-SQLite adapter scan, high-entropy token scan, screenshot-location scan, whitespace scan, and `Leibniz` closure plus graph fix verification with no actionable findings; contradiction fix verification is pending.

- Added a durable direct voice-event bridge for the actual Gemma/Kokoro LiveKit path. The Python voice agent now attaches a stable `voice_agent_event_uid` to every emitted event, keeps the LiveKit data-channel path for live captions, and can also POST the same event directly to FastAPI through a best-effort backend sink so always-on sessions do not depend on a browser tab for durable run events. The voice-event API deduplicates browser and agent submissions by that UID before appending `run_events` or materializing dialogue, and duplicate browser responses recover existing materialized-turn and follow-up hints so the UI can still continue the live voice chain when the agent HTTP sink wins first. - Added local LiveKit bootstrap support for provider-backed voice proof. `docker-compose.yml` now has a `voice` profile that starts `livekit/livekit-server:latest` in dev mode, `.env.example` documents the local dev key/secret boundary, readiness metadata carries the native and Compose commands plus official docs links, and the product voice panel renders each readiness check's evidence, missing env vars, and next action instead of hiding blockers inside JSON. Runtime preflight now also calls LiveKit `RoomService/ListRooms` with a short-lived server token, so non-empty URL/key/secret alone no longer count as verified LiveKit connectivity.
- Closed the `Leibniz` cleanup on LiveKit readiness. `LIVEKIT_CONNECTIVITY_PREFLIGHT_TIMEOUT_SECONDS` is now validated as finite, positive, and <= 30 seconds; LiveKit preflight preserves root or path-prefix URLs for proxied deployments, rejects query/fragment URLs with an explicit readiness error before network calls, and records the probed path prefix in metadata. Validation after cleanup: focused preflight tests passed, `compileall` passed, Next typecheck passed, full Python regression is `283 passed, 10 skipped`, and `Leibniz` found no blockers.
- Added bounded LiveKit audio-turn artifact persistence for real Gemma/Kokoro provider calls. Captured audio turns are stored under `ARTIFACTS_ROOT/voice-audio/...` with artifact URI, relative path, byte count, and SHA-256 metadata; durable voice events and materialized conversation turns carry only metadata, not raw PCM; and the Gemma adapter now still sends inline base64 audio when an artifact URI exists, preventing provenance refs from replacing the actual native-audio payload. The local artifact lifecycle now has retention-day and cleanup-interval settings with opportunistic cleanup. Validation after `Leibniz` cleanup: focused voice/API/provider tests passed, `compileall` passed, Next typecheck passed, full Python regression is `288 passed, 10 skipped`, no SQLite adapter-pattern matches, and screenshot-location scan is clean.
- Wired provider-backed Gemma/Kokoro live smoke to captured voice artifacts. When a run has a materialized user voice turn with local `voice-audio` artifact metadata, the provider-smoke voice-streaming step reads that bounded PCM file, verifies the hash when present, sends inline base64 audio to Gemma, and records artifact URI/path/hash/byte details in the provider-smoke event and ledger. If no usable artifact exists, the step keeps the synthetic silence probe fallback. `Leibniz` found and the slice fixed the long-run recency bug by adding `list_recent_conversation_turns`, plus race-safe artifact IO that skips deleted/unreadable candidates. Validation: focused live-smoke coverage passed, full Python regression is `288 passed, 10 skipped`, Next typecheck passed, no SQLite adapter scan is clean, screenshot-location scan is clean, and final `Leibniz` review found no blockers.
- Surfaced captured-audio smoke proof in the creator-facing Next voice panel. The product UI now extracts the Gemma/Kokoro streaming smoke details, shows whether runtime smoke used a persisted microphone artifact or the synthetic probe fallback, and renders artifact path, size, short SHA-256, and source turn id without exposing raw PCM.
- Surfaced realtime voice timing-ledger details in the creator-facing Next voice panel. The UI now renders measured/missing LiveKit, Gemma, Kokoro, and barge-in stages plus latest-turn latency segments, so a user can see which voice-loop proof is real and which evidence is still absent without opening the internal cockpit or raw JSON.
- Hardened the voice proof panel after `Leibniz` review: smoke and timing proof requests now use a shared run-bound request guard so stale completions cannot update a replaced run, invalid negative latency values render as invalid instead of credible-looking timings, and `npm run test:race` includes an executable stale smoke/timing completion simulation.
- Added local LiveKit dev-server supervision as a product voice transport control. FastAPI now exposes status/start/stop endpoints for native `livekit-server --dev` or supervised foreground Compose mode, the Next voice panel shows `Local LiveKit transport` with Start/Stop/mode controls, and `Join voice room` tries supervised local LiveKit startup before runtime preflight when enabled. `Leibniz` cleanup added force-restart orphan protection, bounded log-line settings, explicit stdout reader-task cleanup, and clearer foreground-supervised versus detached-manual Compose semantics.
- Aligned provider-smoke live voice proof with the same hosted-or-local Kokoro boundary as runtime readiness. The Gemma/Kokoro streaming smoke no longer falsely requires `KOKORO_TTS_ENDPOINT_URL` when the local Kokoro package is available; it records the selected `kokoro_provider` and `kokoro_transport` in durable proof.
- Centralized Kokoro endpoint normalization in `voice_agent/kokoro.py` and reused it from readiness, provider smoke, and the runnable LiveKit participant. The creator-facing voice proof card now distinguishes blocked and failed Gemma/Kokoro smoke from a real synthetic-probe fallback.
- Surfaced provider-smoke transport evidence in the creator app. The runtime smoke card now shows whether Kokoro proof came from an HF endpoint or local package, plus Gemma TTFT, Kokoro first-audio latency, and end-to-end first-audio latency. Frontend provider-smoke statuses are typed as known smoke states, with unknown statuses held as pending/unproven.
- Added backend `ProviderSmokeStepStatus` and `ProviderSmokeRunStatus` enums so provider-smoke ledgers cannot silently emit arbitrary statuses. The contract still serializes as plain strings over JSON, keeping the app API stable while aligning backend and frontend proof semantics.
- Added `KokoroRuntimeRoute` so runtime readiness, provider-smoke blocking details, and provider-smoke live proof all share one hosted/local/missing Kokoro route decision. The product proof helper now includes missing Kokoro route evidence when smoke is blocked.
- Tightened `KokoroRuntimeRoute` to reject malformed hosted endpoint strings before route promotion. Valid hosted endpoints, local-package fallback, missing TTS, and malformed endpoint blockers now produce distinct readiness metadata and product proof text.
- Runtime and smoke streamer construction now fails fast when `KokoroRuntimeRoute` is not ready, preventing missing local Kokoro installs from surfacing only during the first TTS stream.
- Session-bound provider smoke now reuses the active LiveKit realtime session instead of creating a separate proof session, can require fresh `gemma_kokoro_voice_agent_ready` evidence, and blocks before external Gemma/Kokoro calls when participant presence is missing or stale. The creator app passes the active session id for live smoke from a joined Gemma/Kokoro room.
- Review cleanup: session-bound smoke now puts the requested realtime session id, room, and creator participant identity on the actual `RealtimeVoiceTurnInput`; fresh presence lookup uses a targeted ready-event query instead of a generic latest tail.
- Added a Postgres `(run_id, event_type, event_id)` index so targeted presence-event lookup stays practical for high-churn always-on runs.
- Session-bound live smoke now requires a captured user voice-audio artifact from the same realtime session. If the active LiveKit session has presence proof but no persisted same-session user audio yet, runtime smoke blocks before any Gemma/Kokoro external call instead of using the synthetic silence probe.
- Same-session audio fixture matching now accepts older records that lack `realtime_session_id` metadata only when the artifact path itself contains the requested session id, and scans a larger recent-turn window before blocking.
- The path compatibility fallback now requires the session id as an exact path segment, not a substring, to avoid accidental binding from misleading artifact paths.
- Product live-smoke now actively probes the connected LiveKit room before building session-bound provider smoke. `probeAndWaitForVoiceAgentPresence` sends a fresh probe id, polls durable presence for a bounded window, updates the visible participant proof, then lets backend smoke record pass/block evidence. The captured-audio proof card now gives a specific same-session-audio action when smoke blocks on `session_audio_artifact_missing`.
- Review cleanup: Stop invalidates in-flight smoke/timing proof requests, the presence probe wait can cancel when the proof request goes stale, and generic LiveKit presence/event handlers now require the active run plus active realtime session before writing product UI state.
- The product voice panel now exposes the required live voice state machine directly. `frontend/next-app/lib/voice/liveStage.ts` projects LiveKit and Gemma/Kokoro events into disconnected/connecting/connected/listening/thinking/speaking/interrupting/reconnecting/ended/failed, and the UI shows room, mic, agent, and context-pruning signals in a responsive state strip.
- Review cleanup: runtime event callbacks use the active run/session guard before changing the state strip, and reconnecting state is not downgraded by a transient connection-state `disconnected` event.
- The state strip now surfaces server-side cancellation acknowledgement. Interrupt starts as a recorded request, `voice_edge_cancellation_acknowledged` advances to Rust edge acknowledgement, and `gemma_kokoro_voice_turn_cancelled` confirms Gemma cancellation, Kokoro buffer clearing, and LiveKit output stop.
- Review cleanup: a failed control request can only mark a still-pending interrupt as failed, Stop resets stale cancellation proof, and the parser accepts both `drop_outbound_audio` and `drop_outbound_audio_packets` output-stop evidence.
- Manual product barge-in now sends the realtime control where it matters first: the Next LiveKit runtime publishes `voice_interrupt` to `agent.voice.control`, clears local playback immediately, then records the durable control event with the LiveKit control id or failure. The Python participant handles that message, cancels the active Gemma/Kokoro response, and emits `voice_manual_interrupt_received` or `voice_interrupt_no_active_response` for visible acknowledgement.
- Review cleanup: LiveKit control messages are now strictly targeted. Presence probes and manual interrupts are ignored unless they arrive on `agent.voice.control`, include matching run/session ids, and come from the creator participant identity stored in the session state. Regression coverage now rejects missing targets, wrong topics, wrong senders, and wrong sessions before any ready or interrupt event is emitted.
- Stop now uses the same realtime cancellation contract as interrupt. Before disconnecting a provider-backed LiveKit room, the product app sends the agent stop-output control, records durable `stop_output` with `cancel_gemma`, `clear_kokoro_buffers`, and `stop_livekit_audio`, suppresses a follow-up task for plain session stop, and only then disconnects and ends the session.
- Review cleanup: Stop now has a run/session ownership guard before late UI state commits, so a stale stop cannot clear a newer voice session. The backend control API also has explicit regression coverage for `stop_output` with `create_followup_task=false`.
- The connected voice room now has a lightweight liveness monitor. While the provider-backed LiveKit session is ready, the product app periodically refreshes durable participant presence and only sends a new `voice_agent_presence_probe` when proof is missing, stale, or old. Monitor results are run/session guarded and update the visible presence row without requiring the user to run provider smoke.
- Added creator-facing LiveKit microphone mute/unmute control to the real voice panel, with run/session plus sequence ownership guards, disabled rehearsal behavior, visible publishing status from LiveKit local-track state, duplicate-success-log suppression, and executable frontend helper tests.
- Added live voice captions to the creator-facing voice panel. Backend Gemma delta events now carry safe `text_delta` payloads, committed user voice events carry transcript when available, and the product UI shows current You/Agent captions from active LiveKit data-channel events before durable conversation refresh completes. Same-session stale old-response events are rejected by turn/response id correlation.
- Added product-facing local worker-scheduler process supervision for always-on Autopilot. FastAPI now exposes status/start/stop for a run-scoped `run-worker-scheduler --watch` process, the supervisor redacts provider/database secrets and reports run/mode/cadence/log tail, and the actual Next Activity rail shows compact `Local scheduler` state with Start/Stop controls gated on the newest active Autopilot profile. Review cleanup added stale-poll suppression with a control token and aligned scheduler-process cadence validation to the worker-profile `0.25s` floor.
- Added public A2A discovery compatibility without overstating protocol support. `/.well-known/agent-card.json` advertises the studio and skill set as a local HTTP+JSON discovery surface; `/api/a2a` advertises method-aware route records that are checked against OpenAPI. Public A2A modes are limited to JSON/text until raw media and streaming/state-history have public A2A-compatible routes; internal LiveKit/Gemma/Kokoro media modes remain under `x-agentStudio`.
- Added read-only A2A message lookup for local/public compatibility. `/api/a2a/messages/{message_id}` returns the durable `AgentMessage` without appending events or mutating state, and `/api/a2a` advertises it as `getTask` with method/path proof. This is still trusted-local raw message projection; remote exposure needs auth or redaction before payload/result/error should be public.
- Added explicit public projection for A2A message lookup. `GET /api/a2a/messages/{message_id}?projection=public` returns a redacted `AgentMessagePublicProjection` while the default private projection preserves trusted-local raw compatibility. The public projection recursively removes snake_case, camelCase, and token-suffixed sensitive provider keys and redacts Bearer/HF/Tavily-shaped strings from payload, result, error, and handoff trace.
- Added local-first secret-file defaults for provider readiness. `Settings` now looks for `.secrets/hf_token` and `.secrets/tavily_api_key` by default, `.env.example` points to those ignored files, and provider readiness reports non-secret `loaded`, `missing`, `empty`, `unreadable`, or `direct_env` status. Direct env values still override file contents. `.secrets/README.md` is allowlisted while actual secret files remain ignored.
- Made provider-smoke configuration blocker tasks executable by the autonomous worker loop. Inference Systems Engineer and Agent Harness Engineer now handle `review_provider_configuration_blockers` with a deterministic `provider_configuration_recovery` provider-operations ledger, secret-safe blocked-step normalization, owner-routed recovery checks, blocked fallback policy, and deterministic follow-up tasks for Observability runtime health proof plus Agent Harness checkpoint/resume planning. Web-search configuration repair is owned by Agent Harness, while source-grounding recheck stays with Web Research only after configuration is ready.
- Hardened this recovery path for replay and secret safety. Provider metadata redaction now normalizes snake_case, camelCase, compact, nested, and suffix-sensitive keys such as `apiKey`, `rawResponse`, `session_token`, `refreshToken`, and `privateKey`; `provider_configuration_review_recorded` uses an idempotency key so a retry after partial side effects does not duplicate proof events; replayed worker cycles stay idle without duplicate artifacts or child tasks.
- Verified the slice with failing-first provider-configuration recovery tests, focused provider/recovery/provider-smoke tests, targeted A2A/foundation worker tests, frontend race tests, compileall, hygiene scans, and a host-context no-skip backend run: `LIVE_POSTGRES=1 python3 -m pytest -q -rs` -> `454 passed`. `Leibniz` found one additional high-severity durable redaction gap for credential/authorization marker keys, which is now fixed with nested `credentials`, `serviceAccountCredentials`, `bearer`, and `authorizationHeader` regression coverage; final `Leibniz` verification reported no actionable findings.
- Made provider-configuration recovery proof visible in the actual product app. The DraftBoard Proofs view now summarizes `provider_configuration_recovery` provider-operations ledgers with status, provider ids, provider-smoke transport, provider-configuration component, first blocker reason, recovery-check count, required-action count, owner agents, and blocked fallback policy, using the existing compact operational proof card rather than raw JSON. These artifacts remain non-revision targets with no checkbox or Revise action. Validation passed failing-first frontend proof regression, full frontend race suite (`185 passed`), Next lint/build, focused backend provider-smoke/recovery tests (`19 passed`), host-context live Postgres full regression (`454 passed`), hygiene scans, and `Leibniz` no-actionable-findings review.
- Made the product voice release gate recovery-aware for provider-configuration blockers. `provider_configuration_recovery` ledgers now block the same `provider-recovery` gate as realtime provider failures when they are newer than the latest provider-backed live smoke, and only a newer same-session live provider smoke ledger can clear them. The voice setup checklist preserves the `Provider configuration recovery` label and maps it to the same live-smoke resolver action instead of mislabeling it as provider failure recovery. Validation passed failing-first release-gate and setup-label regressions, frontend race suite (`188 passed`), Next lint/build, focused backend provider-smoke/recovery tests (`19 passed`), host-context live Postgres full regression (`454 passed`), hygiene scans, and final `Leibniz` no-actionable-findings verification.

## Working Rules

- For each new feature slice, define the critical test suite before implementation and keep regression/unit/integration coverage proportional to risk. Do not skip critical voice, retrieval, source-ledger, or state-ownership cases even when edge-case coverage is intentionally bounded.
- Send `Leibniz` one complete review packet per coherent slice with enough scope to inspect stale-state, replay/idempotency, secret boundaries, ownership routing, durable-store consistency, concurrency, test adequacy, and bloat in one pass. Follow-up review is for verifying real fixes, not for widening an underspecified first pass.

## In Progress

- Continue hardening the actual creator-facing product app while keeping cockpit/planning as internal/operator surfaces only. The provider-backed live voice proof is accepted for the current OpenRouter (`deepseek/deepseek-v4-flash`) + LiveKit + Kokoro route; do not reopen it as the active blocker.
- Remaining proof gate: external publication proof. Current blockers are LinkedIn credential file/value, LinkedIn policy acknowledgement artifact, durable external destination ID/URL, rollback or postcondition evidence, then accepted proof record and closure review.
- Current recovery handoff: while `external-publication-proof` operator inputs are blocked, current-gate completion commands must start with `provider-proof-operator-input-readiness --fail-on-blocked`, credential snapshot, proof-plan, matrix/status/checklist refresh, and one completion-status recheck. Product/publish preflight capture, `build-distribution-package > distribution-package.json`, proof-record template, record validation, and record audit resume only after operator-input readiness is clear. Accepted live-voice commands must stay excluded.
- Current CLI guard: `provider-proof-completion-status --output-dir <provider-proof-workspace>` now works for custom proof workspaces and reads that workspace's `operator-input-readiness.json` before emitting recovery commands. Leibniz found the final completion-status recheck still dropped the custom output directory; the recheck now preserves `--output-dir` in both top-level and per-proof/current-gate recovery commands.
- Product hardening can proceed in parallel only when it does not mutate proof state or interfere with Cursor/OpenRouter/LiveKit processes: branch-protection/auto-merge proof, manual PR/merge/release follow-through, and future Rust voice-edge concurrency/media-bridge work. The local Ruff baseline, branch-head remote CI was green at the last live check, clean-env Playwright install proof, and ship-gate/bootstrap/provider-proof/CI skills are already present; regenerate exact CI URL and head SHA at PR creation time.
- Treat Gemma/HF/Gamma/MLX setup as legacy/native-audio background, not an active prerequisite for live dialogue. Web-search endpoint configuration remains separate from live voice proof.
- Continue turning system-design-vault chapter scaffolds into compact original notes and Agent Studio implications, with `Practical MLOps` and official agent/eval/security sources next.
